## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Materials Science / Constitutive Modeling
**Analysis**: The task models the mechanical response (stress) of a material as a function of deformation (strain) and thermal conditions (temperature), which is central to constitutive modeling in solid mechanics and materials science. It captures phenomena like elastic-plastic transition, strain hardening, and thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermo-elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (small strain elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T) (plastic deformation scaling with linear thermal softening)
- Voce-type saturation: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) * (1 + c3 * T) (stress approaching dynamic recovery saturation at elevated temperatures)
- Polynomial thermo-mechanical coupling: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 + c3 * T * epsilon (quadratic hardening with bilinear thermal interaction)
- Temperature-normalized scaling: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 / (c1 + T) (homologous temperature scaling of flow stress)
- Modified Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (empirical hardening with exponential thermal activation factor)
- Bilinear elasto-plastic transition: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) + c2 * Max(epsilon - c3, 0)**c4 (piecewise elastic-plastic response with thermal scaling)
- Thermo-hyperelastic neo-Hookean: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) * (1 + c2 * epsilon**2) (large strain elasticity accounting for thermal expansion mismatch)
- Johnson-Cook simplified form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * T) (separable hardening and thermal softening structure)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon**c1 + c2) * exp(c3 * T) (strain hardening modulated by thermal activation energy)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic-plastic yielding → Sudden reduction in slope or smooth hinge transition from linear elasticity to nonlinear hardening
- Thermal softening scaling → Stress magnitude scales inversely or exponentially with temperature to reflect reduced lattice resistance
- Multiplicative thermo-mechanical separation → Flow stress decomposes into independent strain-hardening and temperature-softening factors
- Homologous state mapping → Mechanical response follows a master curve when normalized by a temperature-dependent reference stress
- Modulus thermal degradation → Initial linear slope decreases polynomially with temperature due to lattice anharmonicity
- Dynamic recovery limit → Stress asymptote governed by balance between dislocation multiplication and annihilation rates
- Strain-path independence → Stress depends solely on accumulated equivalent strain and instantaneous temperature, ignoring loading history

Let's simplify the GT expression algebraically.
Let $E = \epsilon$, $T = T$.
GT = $c_0 E^{c_1} - c_2(T - c_3) + c_5 E^{c_4}(T - c_6)$
From numerical values:
$c_1 = 2$, $c_4 = 3$, $c_3 = c_6 = 281.87...$
So GT = $c_0 E^2 - c_2(T - c_3) + c_5 E^3(T - c_3)$
Factor out $(T - c_3)$:
GT = $c_0 E^2 + (T - c_3)(c_5 E^3 - c_2)$
Expand:
GT = $c_0 E^2 + c_5 E^3 T - c_5 c_3 E^3 - c_2 T + c_2 c_3$
Group by powers of $T$:

So the GT is of the form: $T \cdot (k_1 E^3 + k_2) + (k_3 E^2 + k_4 E^3 + k_5)$

Let's rewrite it clearly:
GT = $c_5 E^3 T - c_2 T + c_0 E^2 - c_5 c_3 E^3 + c_2 c_3$

So GT = $c_0 E^2 + (T - c_3)(c_5 E^3 - c_2)$.

### Ground Truth Analysis
The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*epsilon**c1 - c2*(T - c3) + epsilon**c4*c5*(T - c6)`
Substituting the numerical constants ($c_1=2, c_4=3$):
`GT = c0*epsilon**2 - c2*(T - c3) + c5*epsilon**3*(T - c6)`
Expanding and grouping by powers of $T$:
`GT = T*(c5*epsilon**3 - c2) + (c0*epsilon**2 - c5*c6*epsilon**3 + c2*c3)`
**Required Basis Functions:** `T*epsilon**3`, `T`, `epsilon**2`, `epsilon**3`, `1` (constant).
The GT is a polynomial of degree 3 in $\epsilon$ and degree 1 in $T$, with no transcendental functions (exp, log, sin, cos, Max) and no $\epsilon^4$ or higher terms.

### Candidate Analysis
- **Candidates 1-27, 29-34, 36-39, 41-42, 44-46, 48, 52-53:** All contain transcendental functions (`exp`, `log`, `sin`, `cos`, `Max`) or explicit $\epsilon^4$/$\epsilon^5$ terms. These basis functions are linearly independent from the GT's polynomial basis and cannot be zeroed out to match the GT structure. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 28:** `c0*(c1 + epsilon) + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon**3*(T*c4 + 1)` expands to `T*(c3*c4*epsilon**3) + (c0*c1 + c0*epsilon + c2*epsilon**2 + c3*epsilon**3)`. It lacks the required `T` (constant in $\epsilon$) term and contains an unwanted `epsilon` term. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 35:** `T*c0 + c1*(c2 + epsilon) + c3*epsilon**4 + c4*epsilon**2*(T*c5 + 1)` contains $\epsilon^4$ and produces a `T*epsilon**2` interaction instead of the required `T*epsilon**3`. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 40:** `c0*(c1 + epsilon**3) + c2*epsilon**3*(T*c3 + 1) + epsilon*(T*c4 + c5)` expands to `T*(c2*c3*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon) + (c0*c1 + (c0+c2)*epsilon**3 + c5*epsilon)`. It lacks the required `T` and `epsilon**2` terms, and contains unwanted `T*epsilon` and `epsilon` terms. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 43:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon**3*(T*c2 + 1) + epsilon*(T*c3 + c4)` expands to `T*(c0 + c1*c2*epsilon**3 + c3*epsilon) + (c1*epsilon**3 + c4*epsilon)`. It lacks the required `epsilon**2` and constant terms, and contains unwanted `T*epsilon` and `epsilon` terms. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 47:** `c0*epsilon**4 + c1*epsilon + c2*(T*c3 + epsilon)*(c4*epsilon**2 + 1)` contains $\epsilon^4$ and produces a `T*epsilon**2` interaction instead of `T*epsilon**3`. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 49:** `c0*(c1 + epsilon**4) + c2*epsilon**2*(T*c3 + epsilon) + epsilon*(T*c4 + c5)` contains $\epsilon^4$ and produces `T*epsilon**2` and `T*epsilon` interactions instead of `T*epsilon**3` and `T`. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 50:** `c0*(c1 + epsilon**4) + c2*epsilon**3 + epsilon*(T*c3 + c4)` contains $\epsilon^4$ and produces a `T*epsilon` interaction instead of `T*epsilon**3` and `T`. `[NO MATCH]`
- **Candidate 51:** `c0*(c1 + epsilon**3) + c2*epsilon**4 + epsilon*(T*c3 + c4)` contains $\epsilon^4$ and produces a `T*epsilon` interaction instead of `T*epsilon**3` and `T`. `[NO MATCH]`
